          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Problem Description:



<b class="line"><!---->Problem Description:<!----></b>



<br>





This crash occurs in VIZ service which is releated to GPU process.



<span class="line"><!---->This crash occurs in VIZ service which is releated to GPU process.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





1. Analysis



<span class="line"><!---->1. Analysis<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In function `FrameSinkManagerImpl::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy`[1], it didn't check whether the result of find is `std::end` (only a DCHECK),so overflow occusr when using the `end()->second.children.erase`(1). 



<span class="line"><!---->In function `FrameSinkManagerImpl::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy`[1], it didn't check whether the result of find is `std::end` (only a DCHECK),so overflow occusr when using the `end()-&gt;second.children.erase`(1). <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To trigger this overflow, we need to exit the GPU Process. According to the poc and asan log, I have debugged the code and find that when GPU process exited, the map `frame_sink_source_map_`[1] will become empty. But this map will be filled with new element soon, so it's quite hard to trigger. We need to call `UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy` before the map is filled again as soon as possible. 



<span class="line"><!---->To trigger this overflow, we need to exit the GPU Process. According to the poc and asan log, I have debugged the code and find that when GPU process exited, the map `frame_sink_source_map_`[1] will become empty. But this map will be filled with new element soon, so it's quite hard to trigger. We need to call `UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy` before the map is filled again as soon as possible. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Because it's really hard to reproduce, you may need to try my poc.html serveral times to trigger this overflow. Please see the ASAN log for more information.



<span class="line"><!---->Because it's really hard to reproduce, you may need to try my poc.html serveral times to trigger this overflow. Please see the ASAN log for more information.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





```[1]



<span class="line"><!---->```[1]<!----></span>



<br>





void FrameSinkManagerImpl::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy(

<span class="line"><!---->    const FrameSinkId&amp; child_frame_sink_id) {<!----></span>

  // Deliberately do not check validity of either parent or child FrameSinkId



<span class="line"><!---->  // Deliberately do not check validity of either parent or child FrameSinkId<!----></span>



<br>





  // here. They were valid during the registration, so were valid at some point



<span class="line"><!---->  // here. They were valid during the registration, so were valid at some point<!----></span>



<br>





  // in time. This makes it possible to invalidate parent and child FrameSinkIds



<span class="line"><!---->  // in time. This makes it possible to invalidate parent and child FrameSinkIds<!----></span>



<br>





  // independently of each other and not have an ordering dependency of



<span class="line"><!---->  // independently of each other and not have an ordering dependency of<!----></span>



<br>





  // unregistering the hierarchy first before either of them.



<span class="line"><!---->  // unregistering the hierarchy first before either of them.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  for (auto& observer : observer_list_) {



<span class="line"><!---->  for (auto&amp; observer : observer_list_) {<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->    observer.OnUnregisteredFrameSinkHierarchy(parent_frame_sink_id,<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->                                              child_frame_sink_id);<!----></span>

  auto iter = frame_sink_source_map_.find(parent_frame_sink_id);



<span class="line"><!---->  auto iter = frame_sink_source_map_.find(parent_frame_sink_id);<!----></span>

  DCHECK(iter != frame_sink_source_map_.end());



<span class="line"><!---->  DCHECK(iter != frame_sink_source_map_.end());<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  // Remove |child_frame_sink_id| from parents list of children.



<span class="line"><!---->  // Remove |child_frame_sink_id| from parents list of children.<!----></span>



<br>





  auto& mapping = iter->second;



<span class="line"><!---->  auto&amp; mapping = iter-&gt;second;<!----></span>



<br>





  DCHECK(base::Contains(mapping.children, child_frame_sink_id));



<span class="line"><!---->  DCHECK(base::Contains(mapping.children, child_frame_sink_id));<!----></span>

  mapping.children.erase(child_frame_sink_id);   // (1)=> overflow occurs here



<span class="line"><!---->  mapping.children.erase(child_frame_sink_id);   // (1)=&gt; overflow occurs here<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->  // Delete the FrameSinkSourceMapping for |parent_frame_sink_id| if empty.<!----></span>



<br>





  if (mapping.children.empty() && !mapping.source) {



<span class="line"><!---->  if (mapping.children.empty() &amp;&amp; !mapping.source) {<!----></span>

3. Patch



<span class="line"><!---->3. Patch<!----></span>



<br>

I don't know if there is more to it but I ran it a bunch of times with different numbers of poc.html without triggering asan. 



<span class="line"><!---->I don't know if there is more to it but I ran it a bunch of times with different numbers of poc.html without triggering asan. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I did see bad message triggered from browser to GPU that triggers ReportBadMessage [1].  That is followed by GPU process intentionally crash at this CHECK [2] shortly afterwards. There are also numerous bad IPCs from renderer to browser that cause renderer to be killed. That seems to be working fine.



<span class="line"><!---->I did see bad message triggered from browser to GPU that triggers ReportBadMessage [1].  That is followed by GPU process intentionally crash at this CHECK [2] shortly afterwards. There are also numerous bad IPCs from renderer to browser that cause renderer to be killed. That seems to be working fine.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





One thing I didn't see is all of the poc.html running in the same renderer process which since they're all from localhost I was kinda expecting. I'm not sure if having all the poc.html running in the renderer with process_id=5 is key to reproducing or not.



<span class="line"><!---->One thing I didn't see is all of the poc.html running in the same renderer process which since they're all from localhost I was kinda expecting. I'm not sure if having all the poc.html running in the renderer with process_id=5 is key to reproducing or not.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





However, if I run with DCHECKs I can see the same FrameSinkId is registered more than once [3]. Once for a top level renderer from DelegatedFrameHost and then again from EmbeddedFrameSinkImpl [4]. If both places call HostFrameSinkManager::RegisterFrameSinkHierarchy() with the same parent and child FrameSinkIds it would only insert one entry into FrameSinkSourceMapping::children. Calling HostFrameSinkManager::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy() twice would then probably end up in  FrameSinkManagerImpl::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy() twice. The first call would potentially delete the entry from the map at [4] so the second call into FrameSinkManagerImpl::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy() would find frame_sink_source_map_.end().



<span class="line"><!---->However, if I run with DCHECKs I can see the same FrameSinkId is registered more than once [3]. Once for a top level renderer from DelegatedFrameHost and then again from EmbeddedFrameSinkImpl [4]. If both places call HostFrameSinkManager::RegisterFrameSinkHierarchy() with the same parent and child FrameSinkIds it would only insert one entry into FrameSinkSourceMapping::children. Calling HostFrameSinkManager::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy() twice would then probably end up in  FrameSinkManagerImpl::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy() twice. The first call would potentially delete the entry from the map at [4] so the second call into FrameSinkManagerImpl::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy() would find frame_sink_source_map_.end().<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





EmbeddedFrameSinkImpl::has_registered_compositor_frame_sink_ tries to guard against duplicated hierarchy registration/unregistration but that doesn't work if some other piece of code,  namely DelegatedFrameHost, also thinks it's controlling the same FrameSinkId.



<span class="line"><!---->EmbeddedFrameSinkImpl::has_registered_compositor_frame_sink_ tries to guard against duplicated hierarchy registration/unregistration but that doesn't work if some other piece of code,  namely DelegatedFrameHost, also thinks it's controlling the same FrameSinkId.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Not sure if that's exactly the same problem but it seems related. This would only be accessible from a compromised renderer that can make arbitrary calls via the blink::mojom::EmbeddedFrameSinkProvider. 



<span class="line"><!---->Not sure if that's exactly the same problem but it seems related. This would only be accessible from a compromised renderer that can make arbitrary calls via the blink::mojom::EmbeddedFrameSinkProvider. <!----></span>



<br>

According to my analysis, there are two main factors to trigger this overflow:



<span class="line"><!---->According to my analysis, there are two main factors to trigger this overflow:<!----></span>



<br>





1. crash the GPU process,  I think a normal renderer could do this



<span class="line"><!---->1. crash the GPU process,  I think a normal renderer could do this<!----></span>



<br>





2. crash the renderer, there are also other ways to crash the renderer from a normal renderer



<span class="line"><!---->2. crash the renderer, there are also other ways to crash the renderer from a normal renderer<!----></span>



<br>





Considering the difficult to trigger the overflow, I don't find a stable poc which can trigger this overflow with a normal renderer.



<span class="line"><!---->Considering the difficult to trigger the overflow, I don't find a stable poc which can trigger this overflow with a normal renderer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The `CHECK` has ensured that there will no duplicate keys in the map, I think the poc.html use this call to crash the renderer (I also try to use anther way to crash the renderer like %Abort(0), it can also trigger the overflow. But this need `--js-flags="--allow-natives-syntax"` flag). Actually there are no dup keys in map. Here are some debug info when the overflow occurs.



<span class="line"><!---->The `CHECK` has ensured that there will no duplicate keys in the map, I think the poc.html use this call to crash the renderer (I also try to use anther way to crash the renderer like %Abort(0), it can also trigger the overflow. But this need `--js-flags="--allow-natives-syntax"` flag). Actually there are no dup keys in map. Here are some debug info when the overflow occurs.<!----></span>



<br>





After the GPU process crash, we can see that the size of map is reset to zero. If the renderer is crash then, it will run into function ` FrameSinkManagerImpl::UnregisterFrameSinkHierarchy` and find the FrameSinkId(5,3).  FrameSinkId(5,3) is the id of the embed PDF.



<span class="line"><!---->After the GPU process crash, we can see that the size of map is reset to zero. <br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
